Municipal Government Announces Reward Measures for Commercially Operated Vegetable Markets

The Municipal Government previously stated that the urban population is growing and the existing municipal and commercially operated vegetable markets are insufficient to meet the needs of the citizens. It had ordered the six bureaus of Public Security, Public Works, Social Affairs, Health, Land, and Finance to form a Vegetable Market Construction Committee to comprehensively plan and add vegetable markets for supply. It is now heard that the committee, in order to promote the construction of vegetable markets by businessmen, decided at its seventeenth standing committee meeting to formulate eight articles of reward measures for commercially operated vegetable markets in Shanghai to provide full protection for businessmen who invest in the construction of vegetable markets. It has now been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgation. In the future, when the construction of vegetable markets in the city is completed, all floating stalls on the roads will be incorporated, and citizens will have a fixed place to buy vegetables, which is also a good news for the convenience of the people. The reward measures are recorded below: Article 1: Citizens who apply to the Vegetable Market Construction Committee for approval to invest in the construction of vegetable markets in the city, in addition to complying with the rules for banning hawkers jointly established by the four bureaus of this city and paying vegetable market donations, may apply the provisions of these measures. Article 2: When citizens apply to build a vegetable market, the Vegetable Market Construction Committee will discuss the needs of the location and designate the supply area for users. Article 3: After the vegetable market is completed and reported to the competent bureau for acceptance and approval to open, all floating stalls set up on the roads near the vegetable market will be investigated by the Public Security and Finance Bureaus and ordered to move into the vegetable market to operate. Subsequently, stallholders are not allowed to set up vegetable stalls in the designated area. Article 4: Stallholders should pay the monthly rent of the stall as approved by the government on a monthly basis and must not be in arrears. If the stall rent is in arrears for three months, the vegetable market may report to the Public Security Bureau to send police to expel them and recover the owed stall rent, and may also apply to the Public Security Bureau for police escorts to maintain order in the vegetable market in accordance with the rules for hiring police escorts. Article 5: In case of necessity for sanitation matters in the vegetable market, the Health Bureau may be requested to provide free facilities. If stallholders have injuries or diseases, the vegetable market can issue a certificate and also enjoy the most preferential treatment for treatment stipulated by the Health Bureau. Article 6: The tap water used for washing the vegetable market may be calculated at the lowest price in accordance with the preferential measures for water use by public institutions. The Public Utilities Bureau shall order the water company to comply. Article 7: These measures may be amended at any time if there are supplementary matters. Article 8: These measures shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Progress of Business in the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau

Comparison between the 19th and 20th Years

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau has been in charge of water, electricity, transportation, street lights, and advertising in the city, and has also been running the public businesses of the Shanghai South Wharf and the Huangpu River Ferry for four years, and has made considerable progress. The observation of various statistics of the bureau at the end of December of the 20th year can reveal its general outline. 1) Registration Section (A) Water Supply: 17 well drilling companies, an increase of 4 compared with the end of the 19th year; 105 well drilling projects, an increase of 38; 114 water pipe merchants, an increase of 32; 960 water pipe workers and apprentices, an increase of 372; 444 water supply facilities owned by owners, an increase of 56. (B) Electrical: 233 electrical material stores, an increase of 106 compared with the end of the 19th year; 15 electrical appliance installers, an increase of 10; 1,623 wiring electricians and apprentices, an increase of 837. (C) Transportation: 60 automobile companies, an increase of 1 compared with the end of the 19th year; 112 automobile gas stations, an increase of 37; 12,421 automobile drivers, an increase of 2,550; 7,520 automobiles, an increase of 2,004; 70,226 other vehicles, an increase of 7,238; 30,208 ships, an increase of 10,769. 2) Municipal Equipment Section (A) 8,686 street lights, an increase of 1,504 compared with the end of the 19th year; 4,480 square meters of public advertising space, an increase of 112 square meters; 19 newly installed electrical standard clocks, worth 23,600 yuan. 3) Public Business Section (A) 4 Huangpu River long-distance ferries and 3 cross-river ferries, worth a total of 392,000 yuan. (B) 6 ferry wharves, worth 115,000 yuan. (C) 13 Shanghai South Ship Wharves, worth 182,000 yuan. The total length of the shoreline is 683.04 meters.

Women's Temperance Society Aids Beggar Children

Six More Recruited Yesterday

There are always a large number of beggar children at the Waibaidu Bridge in the Shanghai Public Concession, appearing every day, with their faces and figures haggard, dirty and unbearable, in the name of helping to pull rickshaws, and in fact extorting hard-earned money. Pedestrians often feel their suffering, and the authorities do not prohibit it. The Women's Temperance Society, in view of this, and also feeling that if no measures are taken to help these beggar children, it would not only be inhumane, but also harmful to the national system and the people's livelihood, specially sent Li Acai, a beggar child who had been taken back from the bridge for education, to guide the recruiting staff to the beggar's den. The beggar children saw that he was an old friend, and that Acai was well-dressed, and that his behavior was different from before, so they were quite envious. Six beggar children, Fan Azhong, Tong Zhejiang, etc., were willing to abandon their begging life. It is reported that after the beggar children entered the education institute, they have been cleaned up and renewed, and Ms. Liu Wang Liming, the director of the association, personally went to instruct them. In the morning, they enter the Peigong Elementary School in the institute, and in the afternoon, they learn sock weaving and other crafts.

Real Estate Association Studies Tap Water Meter Issues

A reporter from the Guowen News Agency met with Mr. Li Bohan, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Real Estate Association, yesterday to inquire about the recent situation of tap water issues. Mr. Li said, "The dispute between users and the company after the tap water price increase has lasted for more than a year. Now that the pound exchange rate is gradually increasing, the proposal for a second price increase mentioned by the chairman of the water company's shareholders meeting will of course be dismissed, and the proposal to reconsider when the exchange rate reaches two shillings will be realized soon. However, since this is not a permanent solution, it is not the ultimate goal of this association. The abstract of the report by Mr. Hill, the tap water expert hired by the Public Works Bureau, repeatedly stated that the water company's payment of dividends in pounds indirectly causes users to bear the exchange rate risk, which is not appropriate, and is the same as the proposal that this association made to the water company to adopt a silver plan. However, Mr. Hill's estimation method for calculating the water company's property is still difficult to justify. In addition, the water company recently sent a letter to this association proposing a water meter system. A specialized committee has studied this in detail, and another general meeting will be held in the near future to discuss it at length, because its advantages and disadvantages are deeply related to the future water price." The reporter also asked for his opinion on the interim measures for water prices. Mr. Li said, "This association has repeatedly corrected the water company's collection of water charges based on gross rent, which is illegal and unreasonable. The company has now followed the advice to improve. In the future, owners who collect and pay water prices for small companies should calculate based on the net rent received."

Commendable Bravery of Detectives in Arresting Thieves

Zhu Shende, a native of Ningbo, lives by setting up a money exchange stall in the Penglu small vegetable market, and lives at 31 Chunyang Lane, Youheng Road, Sikaizi Bridge. At about 6:30 last night, Zhu and his wife and daughter were having dinner in the living room when five thieves suddenly broke in. Two of them were holding pistols and ordered everyone not to move. One of the thieves immediately stepped forward and took off the wristwatch and gold ring worn on Zhu's daughter's wrist. Three of the thieves went directly upstairs and went straight into the bedroom to search and rob. Zhu Shende took advantage of the thieves' unpreparedness and escaped from the front station to call the police. At that time, Zheng Huaili, a detective from the Jiaxing Road Police Station residing in the pavilion building, was in the room and saw the thieves hurriedly going upstairs. He asked them what they were busy with. The thieves answered that they wanted to talk to the landlord. Zheng knew that something was wrong, so he put on his clothes and waited with a gun. Soon, the thieves went downstairs in a staggering manner because they had found nothing to rob. Zheng also followed them downstairs. The thieves fled in all directions to the front and back households. Zheng followed the three thieves from the back door to the vicinity of the里口. The thieves had become aware and resisted. Detective Zheng immediately fired three shots, hitting one of the thieves in the abdomen. He was arrested on the spot, and the remaining four thieves fled. The police who had been called by Zhu pursued, but nothing was gained.

Encounter with Thieves While Remitting Money at the Post Office

Arrested by Police on the Spot

Thief Sentenced to Two Years of Penal Servitude

A clerk surnamed Shi from the Kang酒廠 on Gongguan Road, sent apprentice Wu Lianghao (16 years old) to remit 40 yuan to Zhenjiang the day before. At about 2:00 PM that afternoon, Wu was holding the banknotes and went to the post office on Tianzhutang Street to pay for the remittance. When he arrived inside the post office gate, he was spotted by Ningbo rascal Yang Decheng, who came up from behind and snatched the banknotes from Wu's hand and ran out the door. He fled south along Tianzhutang Street. Wu chased after him, shouting loudly for a robber. The police officer on duty at station 137 heard the sound and rushed to arrest Yang. Yang threw away the banknotes and fled to the intersection of Yong'an Street. The Chinese policeman from number 569 and the Western policeman from number 155 came on patrol and intercepted Yang. The policeman from number 137 retrieved the banknotes and took them to the police station together. Yesterday afternoon, they were sent to the First Tribunal of the Second Special Court for investigation. First, the police lawyer Gu Shouxi stated the case and prosecuted him for robbery under Article 343 of the Criminal Code. Wu Lianghao also stated the situation of the robbery, and Chinese and Western police officers testified about the situation of chasing and arresting the defendant. Yang Decheng, who was 18 years old and worked in the printing industry, confessed that he was unemployed and poor and had no choice but to rob the plaintiff's banknotes. Judge Ge Zhiqin verified the confession and ordered the police lawyer to debate. He then announced the end of the trial and sentenced the defendant to two years of penal servitude for the crime of robbery. The number of days of detention before the judgment was determined to be offset by one day of penal servitude for two days. The 40 yuan in banknotes were returned to Wu Lianghao to be taken away.

A Concubine Dismissed by Zhu Jinhou Requests Confirmation of Paternity of Her Daughter

Issue in Dispute: Fosterage vs. Biological Parentage

Zhu Jinhou, a salt merchant from Jing County, Anhui, resides at No. 123 Goden Road in Shanghai's western district. He possesses assets worth millions. In the 17th year of the Republic (1928), Zhu was visiting Suzhou when he met Qinglou (originally named Tang Peizhen, currently 22 years old), a courtesan who advertised her services in the Minqingli district of the city gate. Zhu fell in love at first sight and negotiated with the madam to take her as a concubine. An agreement was soon reached, and in the summer of that year, Zhu married Tang as his concubine. He built a gilded residence at No. 8 Zhang Guolao Lane in Suzhou as a place to house his beauty. After living together for over a year, their love suddenly soured, leading to litigation. Tang first sued Zhu for abuse in the Provisional Court. Zhu counter-sued Tang for fleeing with a female child. Following mediation by friends, the lawsuits were dropped, but they separated. An agreement was signed to terminate their relationship as husband and concubine. Zhu paid Tang five thousand yuan as alimony. The agreement was notarized by lawyers Tao Jiachun and Liu Zuwang. The agreement also stated that the daughter Tang was raising (named Pan Jin, four years old) was a foster daughter and was also to be separated from the relationship. Now, Tang has hired lawyer Wu Baoheng to sue Zhu Jinhou in the First Special Court, claiming that Pan Jin is Zhu's biological daughter, requesting confirmation of Pan Jin's parentage. Yesterday morning, Zhou Daren, the civil division chief of the Special Court, opened the Civil Court No. 8 for inquiry. Zhu Jinhou did not attend, but appointed lawyer Qin Liankui to represent him. Tang Peizhen testified, stating that she was 22 years old, from Suzhou, residing at No. 424 Dagu Road. On February 17th at age nineteen, she married the defendant as a concubine and gave birth to Pan Jin on November 13th, who is now four years old. Judge Zhou asked Tang when she became a prostitute. She replied, "At twelve years old." He asked, "Before marrying the defendant, did you have any physical relations with anyone else?" She replied, "Before I was married, I was still a little girl." He asked, "When did you conceive?" She replied, "February 17th." He asked, "Did you have any relations with Zhu before the marriage?" She replied, "In the first month, yes." He asked, "When did your menstrual cycle stop?" She replied, "February 12th." Judge Zhou then questioned lawyer Qin regarding the plaintiff's statements. Lawyer Qin stated that, according to his client, the girl was not his biological daughter, but was brought by the plaintiff when she married the defendant. He did not know her name or origin, hence the reference to her as a foster daughter in the separation agreement. Therefore, he could not acknowledge her. Judge Zhou then announced that the case would be rescheduled for further hearing. At the next hearing, Zhu Jinhou must appear in court, and Zhu Pan Jin must also be brought to the court.

Wanchang Rice Mill Launches Nutritious Rice for Sale

Contains Vitamins

Wanchang Rice Mill, located west of the Eight Immortals Bridge in the French Concession, considers rice an essential staple, and the most important nutrient for the human body is vitamins, followed by protein and fat. The outer layer of rice is rich in vitamins. However, people only seek clean, palatable rice, forgetting the nutritional elements. Rice mills cater to this preference for whiteness, removing the outer layer, causing the loss of vitamins, and leading to diseases like beriberi, stomach, and intestinal problems. The owner of Wanchang Mill, recognizing this, has collaborated with health experts to preserve the vitamins during the milling process, naming it "Nutritious Rice." Its advantages are as follows: (1) Rice Quality: Generally, early rice is excessively loose, and late rice is excessively sticky. Nutritious Rice is blended using appropriate methods to achieve a balance. It is neither loose nor sticky. (2) Rice Color: Specially refined to retain vitamins, it also has a very white appearance, completely identical to the so-called "top-grade white rice" of the past. (3) Efficacy: Nutritious Rice is easily digested in the stomach. In addition to vitamins, it is also rich in protein and fat, preventing beriberi and stomach ailments, while nourishing the body. (4) Affordable: Cheaper than top-grade rice on the market, while having completely equivalent quality, and even more beneficial. (5) Cooking Method: The process is completely the same as with other white rice, except that it is best to rinse the rice one hour in advance. This Nutritious Rice is now available for sale at the factory's retail outlet. You can also place an order by phone at 83036, and it can be delivered.

Zheng Baozhao's New Initiatives

Admonishing Staff to Rectify Railway Affairs

Zheng Baozhao, the head of the traffic departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, has held firm on his determination to rectify railway affairs since assuming office, striving to commercialize the railway. Fearing negligence among staff, he issued a strict admonishment to his subordinates yesterday. He stated that railways are a public utility, and their sole responsibility is to facilitate convenient and comfortable travel and promote commerce. All traffic employees, especially those directly related to the operations, must strive to maintain the cleanliness and hygiene of trains and stations, ensure comfortable travel, and meet all transport needs. If passengers and merchants are unfamiliar with the rules and regulations, they should explain them gently and avoid any negligence or intentional obstruction. Even if matters are important and beyond their authority, they should promptly report the actual situation to their superiors for review. It is essential to recognize that the development of commerce and the enhancement of railways depend on thorough cooperation and understanding between the railway and the business community. This can only be achieved if all traffic employees, from top to bottom, share this understanding and work together. The office has repeatedly issued strict admonishments, and while employees have shown some awareness, they inevitably relapse into old habits over time. Therefore, this notice is issued again, urging everyone to comply. Those in charge at all levels must earnestly supervise and oversee. If negligence persists, once reported or discovered by this office, it will be strictly investigated without leniency.

Resolution of the Shipping Strike at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company

Many Ships Halted, Disrupting Passenger and Freight Transport

Daily Losses Exceed 10,000 Yuan

The crew, stewards, stokers, and sailors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company demanded double pay, which was rejected by Guo Waifeng, triggering a strike. The news was reported yesterday. Although Guo sent representatives to negotiate with the crew, the strike has not been resolved because of the lack of a solid plan. Ships returning to Shanghai on the Yangtze River have joined the strike, taking united action. It is said that both sides have asked Du Yuesheng to mediate, and it is hoped that this issue will be discussed today. The news from yesterday is summarized below.

United Action by Six Departments Yesterday morning, the crew of the ships that went on strike convened a general meeting of all staff from the driving department, engine department, pilot department, steward department, stoker department, and sailor department to discuss their course of action. It was decided on the spot that the staff of the six departments would adopt a united stance. They would continue to perform their duties on board as usual, and would only resume sailing once the requested double pay was received. Before the double pay was issued, no staff member was allowed to negotiate with the company privately. Anyone who resumed sailing privately, disrupting the collective action, would be regarded as a public enemy and would be responsible for the total amount of the double pay. On the spot, the six departments separately drafted a contract for joint action, with each signing and sealing the contract to demonstrate their determination. Petition to the Municipal Government and Party Headquarters After the meeting, representatives from the six departments went to the Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters to request assistance and explain that the strike was a last resort. They submitted a petition, which was accepted by the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters. They were advised to maintain order and refrain from any actions that deviated from the norm. The representatives were satisfied. The original text of their petition is as follows: Petition for Reporting the Matter: It is known that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is notorious for its long-standing malpractices. Although it has been reorganized by the National Government, and three commissioners have been replaced, with the purpose of reorganization announced to the people, those in power have other intentions. They treat the company staff and crew unfairly. For example, at the end of each year, the company staff routinely receive double pay, but the crew alone is excluded. Moreover, there are special bonuses and various bonus schemes. Comparing the two, the company staff receive almost three months' salary more than the crew in a year. Some staff members, even if employed for only four months, with two months of sick leave, can still receive five months' salary. This is just one example, and the rest can be inferred. Therefore, the crew believes that the discrimination is excessive, and the demand for double pay is not excessive. In addition to verbal requests, written requests have been made for two years. Most recently, in November of last year, a letter was sent to the company requesting double pay, and Mr. Li Shenzheng also made the request to the company on behalf of the crew. All were unreasonably rejected by the company. As a last resort, on the 7th of this month, the crew elected representatives to petition the company. Commissioner Guo firmly refused, saying that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is a mess, and he, Guo, would not last long and would soon close the company. Even if he had to sacrifice his position, he would not be able to treat everyone equally. Commissioner Guo has other motives, placing the crew in a desperate situation, leaving them with no means of livelihood. For the sake of dignity and justice, the crew has resolved to continue their daily work as usual, while awaiting the company to issue double pay, and will immediately sail to various ports. There will be no other actions. Therefore, this document is prepared to report the matter, hoping for your review and consideration for the public good.

Company Representatives Negotiate Yesterday morning, Guo Waifeng arrived at the company. Seeing that the strike was growing and the situation was dangerous, he convened a company meeting to discuss the response. Guo entrusted Li Zhenwu, Xie Baosheng, and Yang Ying to negotiate with the crew representatives at the driving department. They stated that Guo Waifeng regretted his rash remarks the previous day, which led to the strike. However, regarding the crew's request for double pay, he could agree in principle, but because the company was in financial difficulty, he proposed that the company issue the crew a half-month bonus instead. He also requested that the ships resume sailing. The crew refused to change the double pay to a bonus and stated that they would set sail as soon as the payment was issued. No resolution was reached. Request for Du Yuesheng's Mediation This matter has been ongoing for two days without a resolution. The crew insisted that they would not resume sailing until their goal was achieved. Yesterday afternoon, after intermediaries ran around and negotiated, the crew publicly elected representatives Xu Wenfang and Qian Yuzhu, etc., to take a public letter from all the staff to Du Yuesheng and Xie Baosheng, requesting them to mediate. The letter stated that the company discriminated against the crew and treated them unfairly. Yesterday, the crew requested double pay, but Commissioner Guo refused, leaving the crew in a desperate situation. It was recently heard that someone was trying to undermine the strike by accusing it of some crime. For the sake of dignity, the crew had no choice but to persevere. They requested Mr. Du to mediate. It is said that Mr. Du Yuesheng has agreed to the crew's request and has agreed to mediate, and will consult with the company officials today to find a peaceful resolution.

Business Losses One Aspect The ships that initially went on strike numbered twelve. Yesterday, the Yangtze River ships Jiangda and Jiangyu, sailing from Hankou to Shanghai, joined the strike upon arriving in Shanghai, taking united action. There are now five Yangtze River ships and nine ocean-going ships that have suspended operations. According to insiders, the resulting business losses are estimated at 13,000 to 14,000 yuan per day. In the past two days, the losses have already exceeded 20,000 yuan. Yesterday, the Xinming and other ships scheduled to depart could not set sail.

Jiangyu Granted Special Military Transport The Jiangyu, which arrived yesterday, was also within the scope of the strike. Later, a telegram was received from the Central Government, ordering the ship to load officers and soldiers from a division stationed in Hangzhou in Shanghai and transport them to Hankou. The division had already been transferred from Hangzhou and could not be delayed. The crew reported this to the association and requested instructions. The association decided that the matter concerned military transport, which could not be delayed. Although it was during the strike, permission should be granted to set sail. With the consent of everyone, the Jiangyu was able to transport the Fourth Division to Hankou. The other thirteen ships were not allowed to sail freely. If the company still insisted, the association was prepared to send representatives to Beijing to petition the National Government.

Crew's Second Declaration The crew's Double Pay Petition Group's second declaration stated that the crew had requested fair treatment from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company through both verbal and written means, but they had been ignored. As a last resort, they launched a petition and declared the circumstances, requesting public judgment. However, the company's baseless arguments have not yet been addressed. They are now being published together as follows. The company's only argument is that the crew's treatment is superior to that of the company staff. However, in reality, the opposite is true. The crew is now publishing the salary figures of both the company staff and the crew for comparison. The public can judge for themselves which is better. The company's commissioner's salary is 600 yuan, with 400 yuan for public expenses. A section chief's salary is 400 yuan, with 200 yuan for public expenses. A deputy section chief's salary is 300 yuan. An engineer's salary is 320 to 360 yuan. A secretary's salary is 300 to 350 yuan. A staff member's salary is 50 to 200 yuan. An advisor's salary ranges from 300 to 400 yuan. The crew's salary is as follows: Captain's salary is 300 to 500 yuan. First mate's salary is 130 to 190 yuan. Second mate's salary is 80 to 130 yuan. Chief engineer's salary is 130 to 180 yuan. Second engineer's salary is 80 to 130 yuan. Third engineer's salary is 80 yuan. Fourth engineer's salary is 50 yuan. Boatswain and helmsman's salary is 42 to 44 yuan. Foreman and fireman's salary is 42 to 44 yuan. Fireman's salary is 37 yuan. All stewards earn only 140 to 160 yuan. Based on the above table, it is obvious which is better. Moreover, the company has five first-class positions, including commissioner, section chief, deputy section chief, engineer, secretary, and advisor. The crew has three: captain, first mate, and chief engineer. How do they compare with the company? For second- and third-class positions, the crew has second mate and second engineer, while the company has staff members. How do they compare? Regarding medical care, the company has a dedicated doctor and a medical department. Company staff and crew should be treated equally. Furthermore, company staff can hold multiple jobs and receive multiple salaries, and even engage in businesses. However, the crew sacrifices family happiness and social status in exchange for a meager salary, barely enough to make ends meet. The company's expenses are covered by the work of these people who barely make ends meet. Yet, it is said that they are not entitled to the same treatment as the company staff. Is there any justice in the world? Therefore, the crew cannot but publicize the facts to request fair criticism and assistance from the National Government to all industries and sectors. Finally, the crew solemnly declares that the reason for disclosing the salary figures is only for comparison purposes to silence the doubters. They have no complaints about the salary levels of any company staff members. Please do not misunderstand. Declaration.

Minutes of the Shanghai Citizens' Association Meeting

Standing Committee Meeting The Shanghai Citizens' Association held its second Standing Committee meeting the other day. Wang Jian'e, Zhou Fuzhang, Wang Zhaocheng, Wang Hanliang, Liu Zhongying, Wang Weiying, Zhang Hengmei, Wu Liangsheng, Chen Binghui, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Xianfang, Zhang Yichen, Tao Leqin, Zhu Zhichun, and Cao Zhigong attended. Wang Hanliang chaired the meeting, and Zheng Dongshan recorded the minutes. The meeting proceeded as usual. (A) Reports: (1) Report on the previous meeting's resolutions; (2) Report on incoming documents. (B) Discussions: (1) Proposal to improve the association's finances to facilitate its work. Resolved: Urge all branches to remit their contributions promptly. (2) Zhang Zilian proposed that the Legislative and Supervisory Yuan should include representatives of the people as members to demonstrate the spirit of cooperation between the government and the people. Resolved: Telegram to the National Government regarding the method of selecting personnel for the Legislative and Supervisory Yuan. (3) Tao Leqin proposed that the current dictatorship is an aristocratic dictatorship oppressing the people's finances. People should be aware that economic power can save the country and restrain the dictatorship. A National People's Economic Conference should be convened quickly, following the German model, to discuss solutions. A unified position is desired to resolve national affairs. Resolved: Wang Zhaocheng seconded the proposal. It is appropriate for the people of the whole country to rise up and organize a financial conference. If this is done, the military will not be used as private property. (Zi) Telegram to the National Government to adopt public opinion and support its establishment. (Chou) Broadcast to the whole country, a unified call for rapid mobilization and organization. Committee member Tao Leqin was assigned to draft the document. Publication of "Zhi Dao Xin Chuan"

The book "Zhi Dao Xin Chuan" was orally transmitted by Zheng Siyuan, a disciple of Ge Xianweng, and recorded by Liu Wenbin. There was a carved version during the Ming Dynasty, but it is extremely rare today and cannot be bought for less than several tens of dollars. The manuscript copy in the collection of the Huang family of Wuxi is treasured by them for generations. Fearing its loss, it is now being reprinted for publication by the Meibaige Road Medical Bookstore. The price is 30 cents per copy, plus 4 cents for postage. Mr. Jiang Zhuzhuang said, "When I was young, I loved to study Taoism and read no fewer than hundreds of Taoist books. Most of them were vague in wording and deliberately obscure, making it difficult for people to understand. Only the book 'Zhi Dao Xin Chuan' is truthful in every word, with absolutely no concealment. If scholars follow it and practice accordingly, they can progress step by step without going astray. It is a raft for saving the world, and students of Taoism should each have a copy."

Reader Correspondence

Three Answers: The National Government Must Be True to Its Name; I Do Not Support Strikes

Trying Out Small Industries: Wang Maoxun

1. Regarding political reform, the politics of the past were still corrupt, which is undeniable. The first and most important thing to do now is to make the National Government live up to its name. Since the establishment of the National Government, how much power have we, the people, actually participated in? How many meetings have been attended by the people? Has our public opinion been adopted? Do we, the people, have the freedom of speech? Therefore, I think the most important thing is to make it true to its name. From now on, the people should participate in a part of the power, and the people should also be qualified to participate in most of the meetings. It is necessary to adopt public opinion and effectively protect the people's freedom of expression. This is what is meant by a real national government. In addition, diplomacy should be transparent, so as not to make the people fall into a fog and not to deceive the people, so that the people lose faith in the government. In addition, the people should have the right to expose officials, whether they are corrupt officials, new warlords, or traitors. As long as they are recognized by the public, the people have the right to eliminate them.

2. Regarding student work, I am a student myself, and I support not striking. Strikes are certainly a sign of high public morale, but I do not support this kind of expression. We must express it in practice. The Prussian army in "The Last Lesson" is already sounding the horn, but the students are still in class. We can know that they were in class before the Prussian army occupied it, and they were also in class during the war. If there is no such calmness, "The Last Lesson" would not be so famous. If there were no such stimulus, France would never have recovered Alsace-Lorraine. I think that for students, there is no more important work than studying. However, studying is definitely not just rote learning. For example, those who study commerce should, when the country is in trouble, desperately study the enemy's commerce and what kind of Chinese goods can be sold well in the Japanese market, and how to make Chinese goods sell well in the international market. Those who study liberal arts should study Japanese culture and other cultural undertakings. As for those who study engineering, they should study science and new weapons to kill the Japanese bandits. In addition, agricultural science and other subjects should all study their own subjects. Now is the time to study, and in the end, everyone will work together to resist the Japanese bandits.

3. Regarding the manufacturing of national goods, regarding this point, I have several classmates who have already engaged in the development of small industries. Now they have raised 1,000 yuan to try it out. First, they will weave belts, shoelaces, and other various shoelaces. In addition, several classmates are preparing to manufacture electrical condensers and ore and other radio parts, because most of the ore and electrical appliances are enemy goods. Enemy goods are cheaper than European and American goods, and our country does not imitate them, and even if they are sold, the price is too high. They are planning (I am also a member). As for whether they can succeed, that is another question. As for other various small industries, as well as enemy goods that are sold well in our country, our country really needs such industrial products. I hope that the people of the country will quickly get up and imitate them and seize the position of enemy goods. (C)

Small Forum

Fortunately, There Are National Goods Stores on Nanjing Road

Walking west from Huangpu Road to the New World, the address numbers indicate that there are a total of 651 stores. Of course, these 651 stores are all kinds of glittering and resplendent shops on Nanjing Road.

Among these 651 stores, purely national goods stores, in terms of clothing, there are only three cotton weaving companies: Sanyou, Samsung, and Anlu. In terms of food, there are only three dim sum shops: Bei Wanxin, Wufangzhai, and Shen Dacheng; two Shaoxing wine shops: Wang Baohe and Wang Yuhe; and three tea and meat shops: Maoshenghe, Bei Wanyouquan, and Jinlan. In addition, there are Darentang Chinese medicine store and Shidezhi medicinal water store, Shuanglong tea shop. In terms of daily necessities, there are only three Jiangxi porcelain shops: Jianhua, Lihua, and Jingde; Chen Jiageng Rubber Shoe Company; and Yichangheng Carpet Shop. In terms of consumables, there are only Guang Shenghang and Pinzhen antique shop. Altogether, there are only 21 stores, which is a percentage of 3.2% out of 651. In addition, there are a few stores that are mostly purely national goods, but unfortunately, they also sell a few imported goods, such as restaurants selling foreign wine, candy stores selling foreign sugar, and fruit stores selling foreign fruit, so they are not included. Perhaps this statistic has omissions and is not entirely accurate, but even the stores listed above inevitably have some foreign elements, such as the cotton used in cotton weaving factories and the flour used in dim sum shops, which are probably still foreign raw materials. If we seriously distinguish them, the national goods stores on such a large Nanjing Road are probably as rare as morning stars. On the contrary, those who purely sell foreign goods probably account for the absolute majority.

According to statistics in 1930 (Republic 19), the total import of rice was 7,138,406 piculs, kerosene was 26,209,028 American gallons, cotton was 2,719,660 piculs, cotton yarn was 8,453 piculs, flour was 223,671 piculs, cigarettes were 1,895,245 (unit: thousand) sticks, coal was 865,365 tons, and sugar was 1,740,228 piculs. As for the import value of Shanghai Port alone, it was a total of 470,231,624 customs taels, while the export value was 312,667,646 customs taels. The trade deficit should be 157,563,978 customs taels. Observing from the above figures, Shanghai is truly a large market for consuming foreign goods. Shanghai people are truly big customers who support foreigners.

Mass Literature and Art

Borrowing Authority

The factory bell rang, and I slowly walked out of the factory. Countless brothers crowded around me, all heading to their respective residences. From afar, I saw a group of people gathered on the roadside. I thought it must be a monkey show, but when I got closer, I realized that it was a White Russian and a rickshaw puller arguing.

"You rode in my rickshaw and didn't pay. What's the meaning of that?" The rickshaw puller grabbed the Russian's arm and sternly questioned him. The White Russian pretended to have the dignity of a proud gentleman, ignored the rickshaw puller, shook off his hand, and walked away. The rickshaw puller became even more angry and rushed forward to grab him again and ask him for money.

"You are really unreasonable. Why don't you pay for the ride?" I was watching from the sidelines and felt somewhat indignant, so I couldn't help but say this.

"Beat him! This is outrageous!" The onlookers shouted. The White Russian saw that the situation was not good and hurriedly took out two dimes from his pocket and threw them on the ground, glaring angrily at the rickshaw puller and me.

"Where are you from? What do you do?" He seemed to want to be impolite to me. At this time, the eyes of the onlookers all turned to me.

"I am Chinese! I am a Chinese worker!"

I said, raising my head to face him.

"I am a Britisher! Do you know that?" The White Russian said this and walked away.

He probably wanted to borrow the authority of the world's great powers to scare me and the general onlookers, but everyone unanimously let out a scornful laugh... "Tch"... "Tch"... "Tch".

North Wind, Yi Nong

North wind, north wind...

Why are you so cruel!

Why are you so stubborn and fierce!

You have already blown through my front screen,

Why do you want to invade my defenseless sickbed?

North wind, north wind...

Are you really heartless?

Can you not have pity on my sick body? (My sick body is probably the sick body of our country)

North wind...

You are truly hideous and cruel.

You have no pity on my sick body.

Not only do you not pity my sickness,

But you also want to end my remaining life!

North wind...

Why do you have to be so fierce!

You should know that you are only taking advantage of the season.

Please tell me, when summer comes, where can your power and whereabouts be seen again?

Written on my sickbed on January 7th (Que Chou)

Mass Science

The People's Science Teacher

What kind of world is it now? It is a motor world, an electrical world, an aviation world, a manufacturing world. In a word, it is a scientific world.

What kind of China is China? It is a poor China, a weak China, a China with low knowledge, a China with thin ability. In a word, it is a scientifically backward China.

A scientifically backward China must quickly promote science and strive to study science. To study science, you must recognize many teachers. Where are the teachers of science? The teachers of science are everywhere.

Confucius had no permanent teacher. He asked about everything when he entered the Grand Temple, and every event became his teacher. He also said, "When three men are walking together, there must be one who can teach me." If there is one teacher among three people, then how many teachers do we have!

As long as we are humble, not only is everyone our teacher, but all things are our teachers. There is a gourd at home, and the gourd is the teacher. There is a bird in the tree, and the bird is the teacher. There is a clock hanging on the wall, and the clock is the teacher. There is a teapot on the table, and the teapot is also the teacher. There are wild animals in the mountains, and wild animals are also the teacher. There is a turtle in the river, and the turtle is also the teacher. Only by observing things can we understand the principles. All things have their strengths. If we see something with our own eyes and do not know how to pursue its uses and subtleties, we are truly not as good as things. China is scientifically backward because those who study science do not regard all things as teachers.

If you don't believe me, look at the apple! Isn't it Newton's teacher? Look at the teapot! Isn't it Watt's teacher? Look at the insects and birds and beasts, which one is not Darwin's teacher?

The masses, heaven and earth are your schools, and all things are your teachers. As long as you ask about everything and pay attention to everything, you can be guaranteed to step into the treasure house of knowledge.

Science Games (Continued)

(3) Guessing Coins Across a Fist: Ask a child to take a few copper coins in his hand at will, without prior notice, and I can guess the number of copper coins he took. I myself take a known number of copper coins (let's say seventeen) and say to the child: "Your fist against my fist, make up ten coins, return your original amount, and I'll have seven copper coins left." After saying this, the two of us stretch out our palms and count, and it will be exactly as said, no matter how many the child takes. The reason is, suppose the number I take myself is 10 + a, and the number the child takes is b. Then the sum of the two numbers is 10 + a + b. After the two stretch out their palms, first "make up ten coins," that is, subtract ten from the sum, and then "return your original amount," that is, subtract b again, so the number "I have left" must be 10 + a + b - (10 + b) = a. In other words, if I have thirteen myself, I will have three left. If I have fourteen, I will have four left, and so on. This method is originally a very simple "algebra" subtraction! (4) Guessing Numbers in Separate Rooms: Ask a child to write any number (but it must be within 105) without telling anyone. In a separate room, first divide the original number by three, and only tell me the "remainder" without saying the "quotient." Then divide the original number by five, and tell me the remainder. Finally, divide it by seven and tell me the remainder. At this time, I can guess the "original number."

Method: Regard each remainder from dividing by three as seventy, each remainder from dividing by five as twenty-one, and each remainder from dividing by seven as fifteen. Add the three remainders together to get the original number. But if the sum is greater than 105, then you must subtract 105 from the sum to get the original number. For example, if the remainder from dividing by three is one, the remainder from dividing by five is one, and there is no remainder from dividing by seven, then the original number is 70 x 1 + 21 x 1 + 15 x 0 = 91. As another example, if the remainder from dividing by three is one, the remainder from dividing by five is two, and the remainder from dividing by seven is three, then the original number is 70 x 1 + 21 x 2 + 15 x 3 = 157. But this number is greater than 105, so the real original number is 157 - 105 = 52. The rest are similar. The reason is that this is derived from the "least common multiple" in arithmetic. Explaining it in detail would be very lengthy, and I am afraid that the children would get bored, so I will omit it for now. (End)

Street Sociology

Fortunately, There Are Non-Profit Electrical Advertisements on Nanjing Road

The electrical advertisements on Nanjing Road, red, green, big, small, Chinese, Western, flickering on and off, are colorful every night, illuminating the street like daytime. However, these advertisements are all flashing, tempting people's eyes. Every word is using great attraction, trying to grab the heart of every passerby. "Pay attention to me, I will supply your needs, I will satisfy you." Every advertisement, every word, seems to be sending out such sweet and moving shouts. Its purpose is entirely for profit, with almost no exceptions.

However, there is an exception here. On the side of the Shuanglong Tea Shop, there is a vertical red electrical advertisement with six large characters. However, it is not for profit. The six large characters are "Namo Amitabha Buddha".

Not for profit, then what is it for? This is a mystery. Or, some people say it is for "saving the world" and for "awakening the world." It is a true reflection of the "compassionate heart" of "my Buddha." Or, some people think it is a kind of "decoration," which is precisely what shows the mottled and bizarre nature of Nanjing Road.

When a worldly-wise, pot-bellied merchant, or an illiterate commoner's gaze, passes by this advertisement, what effect will "Namo Amitabha Buddha" have on him? I think only "Namo Amitabha Buddha" knows.

From All Directions

American Kerosene King Rockefeller Boze

"The most important thing for young people who are taking the first step in life is to have credibility, because this is what creates their personality."

American kerosene king Rockefeller often said this. The Anglo-American confrontation is by no means just a naval competition, but a fierce kerosene war. We see it as almost a total mobilization of the British Empire against a Rockefeller.

The reason why he became the current kerosene king is because the banks all believed in his personal character and credibility and lent him 4,000 yuan to start his business. He often said, "I, Rockefeller, will not be wrong. Credit is my entire fortune." Starting with a monthly income of only five or ten yuan, he never said the word "I." He said, "I am just one of us." Therefore, he who often said "we" could become the authority of modern America, precisely because he was fully qualified.

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (3)

Ancient Sites

Shanghai's history is short. From a historical perspective, it certainly can't compare to other metropolises. Famous historical sites are as rare as morning stars. The more important ones are Jing'an Temple, Xujiahui, and Longhua. These three places can be considered the foremost scenic spots in Shanghai. Beside the ancient Jing'an Temple is an ancient well, which was known in ancient times as one of China's six great holy springs. Every spring, on the birthday of Sakyamuni Buddha, a temple fair is held. The four sides of Jing'an Temple form an extremely lively market. Merchants gather, and men and women are as numerous as clouds. The incense in the temple is blinding, and people rub shoulders on the road. Goods are displayed, especially bamboo wares.

Xujiahui is the former residence of Xu Guangqi, a great scholar of the late Ming Dynasty. Guangqi was born in the forty-first year of Jiajing (1562 AD). He was one of the first Chinese scholar-officials to join the Christian church. He befriended the Westerner Matteo Ricci and learned astronomy, arithmetic, and other sciences from him. Therefore, Guangqi was largely responsible for introducing Western science to China. In the southwest corner of the Xujiahui Cathedral is Guangqi's tomb.

Longhua Town has the Longhua Pagoda, a relic of the Han Dynasty. Some say it is a relic of the Tang Dynasty. In the third month of the lunar calendar, the peach blossoms bloom, splendid and colorful for ten miles, adding to the many scenic spots. Men and women tourists are continuously on the road.

Prelude to Opening the Port

In the twentieth year of Qianlong, after the British had conquered India, Biggs of the East India Company had already suggested opening Shanghai to trade. In the eleventh year of Daoguang (1832 AD), the East India Company dispatched the merchant ship Amherst from Macau, with Lyndsay (Mr. Hngh Hamilton Lindsay) as the leader of the commercial committee. Via Xiamen, Fuzhou, and Ningbo, they requested trade, but were refused by all the local authorities. They then went to Shanghai. The Shanghai authorities had known about this and initially wanted to refuse the Amherst merchant ship entry into the port. However, Lindsay managed to find ways, and met with the Shanghai Daotai at the Tianhou Temple. Although he did not receive preferential treatment, he was finally able to state his intentions. The Shanghai Daotai informed him that Guangzhou was the only port open for trade, and that Shanghai could not allow them to stay for long and should leave immediately. Lindsay, unable to get what he wanted, led the ship to Korea. This episode can be considered the prelude to Shanghai opening as a port.

Page 18

A Brief History of the Actors' Association

The Shanghai Actors' United Association is a professional organization formed by all the actors in Shanghai. It was established in the first year of the Republic of China. The purpose of the association is to connect colleagues' feelings, strive for the dignity of actors, and protect the professional status of actors. At the beginning of its establishment, it received support from all walks of life. At that time, in view of the large number of actors' children who were out of school, Zhenling School was established. Furthermore, because actors are also part of the nation, they should have the responsibility to defend the country, so the Actors' Business Corps was founded. During the Xinhai Revolution, they followed the martyr Chen Qimei in attacking and capturing the Manufacturing Bureau, maintaining local security. Their work was very diligent. During the Guichou Revolution, the Actors' Association was resented by the Yuan government for supporting the revolution and was illegally dissolved. The school was also abolished, and the association's address was occupied by military police. In the ninth year of the Republic of China, after the association and the authorities fought hard, the association's premises were finally recovered. The Actors' Association was then revived. The school was also restored. In the eighteenth year, the president system was changed to a committee system. All association affairs were handled by the executive and supervisory committee members. The association's affairs became increasingly complex, and the financial needs also increased day by day.

The Economic Situation of the Actors' Association

The members of the various committees of the Actors' Association are purely volunteers and never receive any subsidies from the association. This is unique to any public organization. The main expenses of the association include the following:

Zhenling Primary School ...... Tuition is completely free for children of colleagues, and books and supplies are also provided. Poor children from outside the industry can also receive free education if introduced by a member. There are currently more than 200 students. Due to the limited school site, students who have registered beyond the quota cannot be accepted, which is a great pity.

Liyuan Cemetery ...... The old cemetery was located on Kangdi Road in the French Concession. Recently, because the surrounding area has become more prosperous, it is not suitable for burial. It has been moved to the Zhenru Township Cemetery. It has more than ten acres of burial land. All deceased colleagues and their families can be buried here without charge.

Nursing Home ...... Acting is a labor-intensive profession. It is not like other professions where experience and qualifications can be relied upon. Therefore, colleagues who are old and weak cannot work. Those who have no children to support them and who have no ability to support themselves, the association has set up a nursing home to take care of them until they die. The home is located in Zhenru Township. Food, clothing, and shelter are all provided by the association.

Changsheng Society ...... When members of the association or their family members die, and they are too poor to afford a coffin, the Changsheng Society attached to the association provides a coffin. All coffins and shrouds are provided by the association free of charge.

Widows' Allowance ...... After a member dies, leaving behind a widow and orphans who have no way to live, the association provides a monthly food allowance at its discretion.

Unemployment Relief ...... During the hot summer and cold winter, the association provides subsidies to poor comrades after investigation, to help them make a living.

Travel Assistance ...... Most of the colleagues in our industry are from out of town. Occasionally, they are in trouble in this city or stranded in a foreign country. Once a colleague reports it, the association provides travel assistance at its discretion to help them return home.

The above are just the major items. Other expenses such as the salaries of hired employees, the expenses of the Liyuan Public Newspaper, and all miscellaneous and temporary expenses of the association are not included.

The expenses of the Actors' Association are huge, but the income and funding come only from two items: members' income donations and Changsheng Society donations. Income donations mean that all members must pay 5% of their monthly salary to the Actors' Association, called the 5% donation. Changsheng Society donations do not specify an amount, and their use is limited to providing coffins and shrouds. Therefore, the association's income and funding is only the 5% donation. With limited income to cover dozens of times the expenses, the association's finances are often stretched, and it has to rely on external assistance.

Fundraising by Performing Drama

The members of the Actors' Association are all working class people who rely on their skills to make a living. If they want to raise funds, there is no other way than to gather all the members to perform dramas together. This is why the association has held large-scale performances in the past. The association has always received support from society, and the Actors' Association's performances are enough to attract audiences. Whenever there are public welfare and charitable events in the local area, there are always performances to raise funds. Each time, the funds raised are considerable. Now, the association is performing for its own fundraising, and it has to rely on the support of philanthropists from all walks of life. In the past, the association did not issue tickets in advance for its performances. Only by using the strength of all the members to perform good plays that connoisseurs have never seen before, can we convey social sympathy and sincerely invite ladies and gentlemen to come. After they come, we must make everyone happy, so that everyone can not only enjoy the pleasure of listening and watching, but also reap the practical benefits of doing good deeds. Therefore, every performance is full of distinguished guests and praised as a grand event in the Liyuan (theater) world. Those who love to talk about the anecdotes of the Liyuan world cannot help but participate in the fundraising performances of the Actors' Association.

The Special Features of the 22nd Grand Performance

The Actors' Association's previous performances were mostly from within the industry. This time, however, Mrs. Du, a famous lady from Shanghai, has been specially invited to join. This shows that her artistic skills are so exquisite that they are admired by all members of our industry. Mrs. Du is not one to easily show her face. This time, because it concerns the public welfare of the acting world, she finally agreed to come on stage after repeated requests from the association. She will perform her masterpiece, the complete play "Crying at the Ancestral Temple." In order to make this play as perfect as possible, the association has specially invited all the famous actors to play supporting roles. This is an unprecedented initiative and a beautiful story in the Liyuan world. This is an unprecedented feature in the Actors' Association's performances. The opportunity will not come again. It is hoped that all lovers of opera will not miss it. As for the highlights of "Crying at the Ancestral Temple," more details will be announced tomorrow.
